<userid>106706847716711523776<//userid><name>Sheila Hamilton< /name><time>1610567877452</time><rate>4</rate>< Text>
First time here and will definitely not be the last. Definitely a community gathering place. They have some great beer on tap with boots! I had the potato apple sauce, pork sausage sauerkraut mashed potatoes, beef with cranberry sauce and red radish. Everything was very delicious although unique for me since I hardly ever eat German food, but it was very tasty and a good change of pace. This is a good place to take friends and dates if you're looking for a solid place to eat and drink.< /Text>

Finally tried this place! I live just down the street and have always wanted to check it out but it's so under the radar I've forgotten. Walking in it's super packed with tables and chairs and it feels like a true home atmosphere. Proportions are huge and the price is about right for what you pay for. <rate>1<//rate><review>NOT PROFESSIONAL QUALITY IMAGES. BELOW AVERAGE, and cell phones yield far better images. It is all about whether the photographer understands their settings. I never thought I would say that Lifetouch takes wonderful school pictures, until my daughter's school switched to Studio 1 last year.  The images are consistently bad quality, not even remotely professional.  Last year, besides having an unpleasantly bright face from what appears to be on-camera flash, the camera lens' focus was on my daughter's shirt, so her eyes were a bit blurry.  We had her retake, and the retake was not great, but better than blurred eyes.  This year, the flash on her face was even brighter, and when retakes were done, her face was even more unusually and unpleasantly brighter than the last image (and her hair wasn't looked into by the photographer).  Any company offering professional photography services should know that a  simple inexpensive diffuser is needed to make the flash emit more natural and appealing results, instead of an unusually bright face. <Review>Why do I only get to give five stars?  I wanna post 6!  Moved here about a year ago and went searching online for a new dentist as needed to replace an implant.  Picked Doctor Vartabedian from the choices I found and couldn't be happier.

Before I get into the quality of the work (stellar) let me talk about "the rest of the stuff."  Staff: beyond professional, helpful and friendly.  Facilities:  state of the art. Information:  lots of it; in addition to whats going on in your mouth, they provide options, right down to specialist recommendations ("if you want the best implant surgeon go to Doctor Jay Uemura").

Now, quality of work: easily as good as you can find anywhere.  State of the art equipment and staff trained in its use.  I walked in to get two crowns and walked out a couple hours later with perfect, beautiful permanent crowns for less than I paid for my other crown some years ago that had a two week wait and needed adjustments. I'm usually pretty hard to numb up, but that wasn't an issue, nor did he need to numb the whole side of my face.

I picked Paul because he was a Prosthodontist, and was pleased to discover he does "regular" dentistry too. Oh, and this morning, he called to check on how my crowns were doing.<//Review>< pics>

<Review>I've been coming to this restaurant since it first started out as a taco truck called "A Que Taco" parked outside of the Safeway market on Indiana (Now El Superior). That was over 30 years ago. The green Chile roasted pork burrito is my absolute favorite dish.  It is quite delicious & huge!  You can split the burrito in half and eat it for dinner.  However,  if you don't want anything too heavy,  my other favorite is the chicken tostada!  It's also very flavorful and filling.  The chicken mole is also very delicious and so are the tacos of Carne asada. Basically every dish is fresh & made to order.  This is one of the best Mexican restaurants in Boyle Heights!< /Review>< Pics>

<Time>1528092451802<//Time><rate>5</rate>< text>
Tucked away in the Santa Clara Caltrain station, this museum has some amazing artifacts from the last 100 years. Its all about trains: the equipment, the routes, the engines. Some great old photos and a replica waiting room. The real treasure in my opinion is the full room miniature city with model trains running throughout. Scenes are set up showing a lot of American history and how trains helped build this country. So fun seeing all this. They are only open 2 days a week, but i think its worth the trip.<//text>

< Review>
This is a great experience for the entire family. An original Railroad Station on the Caltrain line. Inside you will find the greatest (and largest) model train layout I have ever seen! Lots of items on display, great volunteer staff who have great railroad stories and the history of the museum. This is a Must See! Check hours on their website and as far as I know-FREE (you can always put something in the donation jar).< /Review>

< Rate>
5<//Rate>
< review>
Cute hidden camouflaged train museum with lots of electric toy trains on what looks like hundreds of feet of train tracks going back and forth and through tunnels and by miniature towns of various periods representing the local regions and further away. Many old signages and sturdy lanterns, a grand sounding bell you can ring and lights to play with.  It's even possible to rent the facility to use with your own trains. Historic material available on trains, train conductors, train stations, uniforms, train companies,  and the various technologies used.
BE AWARE,  it's not obvious the museum is there,  even when you are standing a foot away from it's main entrance door or rear entrance door, which is a big brown sliding door that's normally closed and you'll need to open it yourself and close it after entering.   The building looks like it's  just an old unused building that's part of the Santa Clara train station.< /review>

< review>
I've been craving a Pulled Pork and Slaw Sandwich for awhile. I've tried other BBQ places in town and wasn't all too happy with the food. We just moved to this area of town and decided to give it a try, especially after reading the owners' bio/experience. I've ate at other restaurants that he was a Chef at and knew I couldn't go wrong.

When I walked into Big D's, I was hit with the typical smell of a BBQ joint located in the South. I ordered the Pork & Slaw Sandwich with a side of Potato Salad to go. Needless to say, I was brought back to my experience of my first Pulled Pork Sandwich in Memphis in the late 1970s. It was DELICIOUS and to die for! And, I love their Slaw. It's an oil/vinegar dressed slaw with tiny bits of green apple. That's very much a Southern thing! The Potato Salad was top notch also. It had bits of chopped black olives with a mayo/mustard dressing. Also DELICIOUS!

I would highly recommend Big D's for a BBQ Joint. It's clean, the staff was courteous and service was fast. I will be a regular there. Next time I have to try their Fried Okra.<//review>

Paid extra for 2 meat meal, brisket & pork.  Brisket was so dried out I mashed fork full in my fingers....no juice.  My fingers were literally dry.  The pork was so overcooked it was mush.  You could mash it like potatoes with plastic fork.  My BBQ beans with cheddar cheese on top?  Beans were still crunchy inside...They did let me exchange them for French fries.  Out of Mac & cheese & other sides.  Also announced out of beans after getting mine sent back.  The owner brought the fries to our table and I mentioned the issues including the dry brisket, she calmly said do you want gravy or sauce to put on it?  No concern for anything..just like oh well.
The cashier said "we've only been open for a month and were still trying to figure out the recipes.  It's hit & miss"  $35 later for 2 meals, the best thing was the bagged frozen French fries and powdered instant mashed potatoes & gravy.  We will definitely be making the trek to North Bakersfield to Dicky's when we go out for BBQ.  What a disappointment.</Review>
